# etcd Error Handling Code Overview

This Go file from the etcd project implements comprehensive error handling for gRPC operations. Here's the complete pattern:

## Error Creation Pattern

The file defines two categories of errors:

**Server-side errors** (gRPC status errors):
```go
ErrGRPCEmptyKey = status.Error(codes.InvalidArgument, "etcdserver: key is not provided")
ErrGRPCKeyNotFound = status.Error(codes.InvalidArgument, "etcdserver: key not found")
// ... and ~50 more error definitions
```

**Client-side errors** (wrapper errors):
```go
ErrEmptyKey = Error(ErrGRPCEmptyKey)
ErrKeyNotFound = Error(ErrGRPCKeyNotFound)
// ... corresponding client-side wrappers
```

## Error Mapping

A central map bridges gRPC and client errors:
```go
errStringToError = map[string]error{
    ErrorDesc(ErrGRPCEmptyKey): ErrGRPCEmptyKey,
    ErrorDesc(ErrGRPCKeyNotFound): ErrGRPCKeyNotFound,
    // ... all error mappings
}
```

## Custom Error Type

```go
type EtcdError struct {
    code codes.Code
    desc string
}

func (e EtcdError) Code() codes.Code { return e.code }
func (e EtcdError) Error() string { return e.desc }
```

## Core Functions

**Error() conversion function**: Translates gRPC errors to EtcdError instances by looking up error descriptions.

**ErrorDesc() extraction function**: Retrieves message text from gRPC status errors or falls back to standard error strings.

This pattern enables consistent error handling across gRPC boundaries while maintaining type safety.

# etcd RPC Error Types Overview

This Go file from the etcd project (Apache License 2.0) defines a comprehensive error handling system for gRPC communications.

## Error Creation Patterns

The file establishes two parallel error hierarchies:

**Server-side errors** use gRPC status codes:
```go
ErrGRPCEmptyKey = status.Error(codes.InvalidArgument, "etcdserver: key is not provided")
```

**Client-side errors** wrap the server errors:
```go
ErrEmptyKey = Error(ErrGRPCEmptyKey)
```

## Error Categories

The definitions cover multiple domains:

- **Data operations**: Key/value validation, lease management, compaction
- **Cluster management**: Member configuration, learner promotion, version mismatches
- **Authentication**: User/role management, permissions, token validation
- **Server state**: Leadership, availability, corruption detection
- **Cluster downgrades**: Version format validation and progress tracking

## Error Mapping

A `errStringToError` map enables bidirectional conversion between error descriptions and error objects, facilitating serialization/deserialization across RPC boundaries.

## Custom Error Type

The `EtcdError` struct wraps gRPC codes and descriptions, with helper functions (`Error()` and `ErrorDesc()`) managing conversion between standard Go errors and etcd's structured error format.

# Error Handling Patterns in v3_server.go

Based on the etcd v3_server.go source code, here are the key error handling approaches:

## 1. **Error Returns from Raft Operations**
The code consistently wraps raft request execution with error checking:
```go
resp, err := s.raftRequest(ctx, pb.InternalRaftRequest{Put: r})
if err != nil {
    return nil, err
}
```

## 2. **Context-Based Error Handling**
Functions utilize context cancellation and timeouts:
- "case <-cctx.Done()" patterns capture deadline exceeded and cancellation scenarios
- The code distinguishes between `context.DeadlineExceeded` and `context.Canceled` errors

## 3. **Retry Logic with Exponential Backoff**
The `LeaseRenew` function demonstrates retry patterns with throttling:
```
time.Sleep(50 * time.Millisecond)
```
Multiple retry attempts occur before returning timeout errors.

## 4. **Error Type Checking**
The code uses `errorspkg.Is()` to check specific error types:
```
if errorspkg.Is(err, lease.ErrLeaseNotFound)
```

## 5. **Sentinel Error Values**
Custom errors from the etcdserver package (e.g., `errors.ErrTimeout`, `errors.ErrStopped`) provide domain-specific error information.

## 6. **Deferred Cleanup on Error**
Password clearing in authentication: "defer func() { if r != nil { r.Password = "" } }" protects sensitive data even during error paths.

# etcd Error Types Overview

This Go source file from the etcd project (Apache 2.0 licensed) defines error handling for gRPC communications. Here's what it contains:

## Server-Side Errors
The file declares numerous `ErrGRPC*` variables using gRPC status codes, covering categories like:
- **Argument validation**: "etcdserver: key is not provided"
- **Resource constraints**: "etcdserver: mvcc: database space exceeded"
- **Lease operations**: Lease not found, already exists, TTL too large
- **Cluster management**: Member conflicts, learner issues, ID mismatches
- **Authentication**: User/role errors, permission denied, invalid tokens

- **Downgrades**: Version format and target validation errors

Client-facing equivalents map to the server errors, providing a consistent interface through wrapper functions.

## Key Functions
- **`Error(err error)`**: Converts gRPC errors to `EtcdError` struct instances
- **`ErrorDesc(err error)`**: Extracts message descriptions from gRPC status errors
- **`EtcdError` struct**: Contains gRPC code and description fields with accessor methods

The file uses an `errStringToError` map for bidirectional error lookup, enabling consistent error handling across server and client boundaries.

# Grafana Error Handling Patterns

Based on the documentation provided, here are the key error handling patterns in Grafana:

## Error Declaration Pattern

Grafana uses a custom error type (`errutil.Error`) built on Go's standard `error` interface. Services declare error categories using status-specific constructors:

- `errutil.NotFound()`, `errutil.BadRequest()`, `errutil.ValidationFailed()`
- `errutil.Internal()`, `errutil.Timeout()`, `errutil.Unauthorized()`
- `errutil.Forbidden()`, `errutil.TooManyRequests()`, `errutil.NotImplemented()`

Each constructor accepts a `messageID` (format: `<servicename>.<errorIdentifier>`) and optional settings.

## Core Construction Approach

**Base errors are declared globally:**
```
var ErrBaseNotFound = errutil.NewBase(errutil.StatusNotFound, "main.notFound", 
  errutil.WithPublicMessage("Thing not found"))
```

**Instances use `.Errorf()` method** (similar to `fmt.Errorf`):
```
return nil, ErrBaseNotFound.Errorf("specific context: %w", wrappedErr)
```

## API Response Handling

The documentation specifies that "API handlers use the `github.com/grafana/grafana/pkg/api/response.Err`" 
function to create responses. However, **the provided content does not include gRPC-specific patterns or detailed HTTP conversion examples**—only references to the `errutil` package's GoDocs for complete implementation details.

**Note:** Detailed gRPC and HTTP conversion patterns are documented elsewhere in the codebase.

# Error Handling Patterns in interceptor.go

This etcd file demonstrates several error handling approaches:

## Early Return Pattern
The interceptors use early returns for validation failures:
```
if !api.IsCapabilityEnabled(api.V3rpcCapability) {
    return nil, rpctypes.ErrGRPCNotCapable
}
```

This pattern "rejects requests before processing when capability checks fail."

## Conditional Error Checking
Metadata validation includes UTF-8 string verification: "if !utf8.ValidString(ver)" triggers an invalid client API version error, preventing malformed data propagation.

## Context-Based Error Preservation
The `cancellableContext` type wraps standard contexts to preserve specific cancellation reasons. Its `Cancel(reason error)` method stores the error before triggering cancellation, allowing downstream code to "disambiguate the reason for the cancellation."

## Leader State Monitoring
The `monitorLeader` goroutine implements graceful degradation. It tracks consecutive election timeouts without a leader, only canceling active streams after exceeding `maxNoLeaderCnt` (3) thresholds rather than failing immediately.

## Deferred Cleanup
Stream interceptors use deferred functions to guarantee resource cleanup:
```
defer func() {
    smap.mu.Lock()
    delete(smap.streams, ss)
    smap.mu.Unlock()
}()
```

This ensures streams are removed from tracking even if handler execution fails.

# Error Handling Patterns in auth.go

This etcd authentication module demonstrates consistent error handling approaches:

## Primary Pattern: Error Wrapping and Conversion

The dominant pattern delegates business logic to an underlying authenticator, then converts errors to RPC format:

```go
resp, err := as.authenticator.AuthEnable(ctx, r)
if err != nil {
    return nil, togRPCError(err)
}
return resp, nil
```

This pattern repeats across all 16+ RPC handler methods, showing a "call-and-convert" strategy where domain errors become gRPC-compatible errors through `togRPCError()`.

## Permission Verification Pattern

The `AuthAdmin` type implements defensive checking:

```go
authInfo, err := aa.ag.AuthInfoFromCtx(ctx)
if err != nil {
    return err
}
return aa.ag.AuthStore().IsAdminPermitted(authInfo)
```

This chains validation—first extracting auth info, then verifying admin privileges—allowing failures at each stage to propagate.

## Key Characteristics

- **Error translation**: Domain errors convert to RPC errors for client communication
- **Early returns**: Errors exit immediately rather than continuing
- **Separation of concerns**: The RPC layer delegates authentication logic elsewhere, minimizing error handling complexity at this level

# Error Utility Functions in etcd's v3rpc Package

This code provides error translation and handling utilities for etcd's gRPC server implementation.

## Primary Function: `togRPCError`

The main function converts internal etcd errors to gRPC-compatible errors:

```go
func togRPCError(err error) error {
	// let gRPC server convert to codes.Canceled, codes.DeadlineExceeded
	if errorspkg.Is(err, context.Canceled) || errorspkg.Is(err, context.DeadlineExceeded) {
		return err
	}
	grpcErr, ok := toGRPCErrorMap[err]
	if !ok {
		return status.Error(codes.Unknown, err.Error())
	}
	return grpcErr
}
```

This function checks a comprehensive mapping (`toGRPCErrorMap`) containing dozens of error translations covering membership, storage, authentication, and cluster-related issues. "If an error isn't in the map, it returns `codes.Unknown`."

## Supporting Utilities

**`isClientCtxErr`** — Determines whether an error originated from client-side context cancellation or deadline expiration, handling both standard gRPC codes and TLS-specific disconnection scenarios.

**`isRPCSupportedForLearner`** — Validates which RPC operations learner nodes may execute; "in v3.4, learner is allowed to serve serializable read and endpoint status" per the inline comment.

These functions work together to ensure consistent error handling across etcd's distributed system operations.

**Core Options:**
- Custom codec implementation for message serialization
- TLS credentials when provided: `grpc.Creds(credentials.NewTransportCredential(tls))`
- Message size constraints: max receive set to `s.Cfg.MaxRequestBytesWithOverhead()` and max send to `maxSendBytes` (Int32 max)
- Concurrent stream limit: `grpc.MaxConcurrentStreams(s.Cfg.MaxConcurrentStreams)`

**Interceptor Chain:**
The system implements layered request handling through:
- Logging interceptor (unary)
- Prometheus metrics interceptor (unary and stream)
- Custom business logic interceptor (unary)
- Optional external interceptor (unary)

**Distributed Tracing:**
When enabled, OpenTelemetry instrumentation is added: `grpc.StatsHandler(otelgrpc.NewServerHandler(...))`

## Error Handling

**Metrics Registration:**
The code demonstrates graceful error handling for metrics registration. If registration fails, the system logs a warning rather than crashing: `lg.Warn("etcdserver: failed to register grpc metrics", zap.Error(err))`

**Service Registration:**
Multiple service handlers are registered including KV, Watch, Lease, Cluster, Auth, Health, and Maintenance servers, each potentially managing their own error states through their implementations.

# Error Handling Patterns in health.go

## Panic on Invalid State

The code demonstrates defensive programming by panicking on unexpected conditions:

> "if hs == nil { panic("unexpected nil gRPC health server") }"

This pattern fails fast when a critical dependency is missing, preventing silent failures downstream.

## Feature-Gated Behavior

Rather than throwing errors, the notifier uses feature flags to conditionally enable functionality:

```go
stopGRPCServiceOnDefrag: s.FeatureEnabled(features.StopGRPCServiceOnDefrag)
```

This approach avoids error states by making behavior configurable at initialization.

## Logging Over Exceptions

The code doesn't throw exceptions for state changes. Instead, it logs events at appropriate levels:

- **Info level** for normal operations (`startServe`)
- **Warning level** for degraded states (`stopServe` with reason parameter)

This pattern treats service status transitions as observable events rather than error conditions, enabling monitoring without exception-based control flow.

## Graceful Degradation

When defragmentation is active, the service transitions to `NOT_SERVING` rather than crashing, allowing clients to detect unavailability through health checks.

# HTTP Response Error Handling in Grafana

Based on the provided code, here are the key error handling functions:

## Primary Error Handlers

**Error()** - Creates standard HTTP error responses with customizable messages and status codes. Returns a `NormalResponse` with JSON formatting.

**Err()** - Converts `errutil.Error` types into HTTP responses, extracting the appropriate HTTP status from the error's reason field and returning public error data.

**ErrOrFallback()** - Intelligently handles three scenarios: uses `errutil.Error` details when available, returns a canceled request response for `context.Canceled` errors, or falls back to provided status/message parameters.

# HTTP Error Handling Utilities in etcd

This code from the etcd project provides two key utility functions for managing HTTP responses:

## `allowMethod()`
This function validates HTTP method requests. It checks if the incoming request method matches an expected method. If there's a mismatch, it sets an "Allow" header and returns a 405 Method Not Allowed response.

## `writeError()`
This function handles error logging and response writing with sophisticated error type discrimination:

**Error Type Handling:**
- **v2error.Error**: Writes directly to the response
- **httptypes.HTTPError**: Writes HTTP-formatted error responses with debug logging for write failures
- **Generic errors**: Maps to HTTP 500 Internal Server Error

**Contextual Logging:**
The function uses Uber's zap logger to distinguish error severity levels. Specific etcd errors (timeouts, connection loss, membership issues) receive warning-level logs, while unexpected errors are flagged separately. Client remote address information is included for diagnostic purposes.

The error handling demonstrates defensive programming—failures during error response writing itself are caught and logged to prevent silent failures.

# Error Handling Patterns in codec.go

This code demonstrates a **minimal error handling approach**:

## Key Pattern

The codec implements two methods that propagate errors rather than handle them:

1. **Marshal method**: `"b, err := proto.Marshal(v.(proto.Message))"` - Returns the error directly to the caller without attempting recovery or logging.

2. **Unmarshal method**: `"return proto.Unmarshal(data, v.(proto.Message))"` - Passes through any marshaling errors without intervention.

## Characteristics

- **Pass-through pattern**: Errors bubble up to calling code rather than being suppressed or transformed
- **No defensive checks**: No validation of input types before casting (`v.(proto.Message)`)
- **Metric recording regardless**: Byte counts are tracked via `sentBytes.Add()` and `receivedBytes.Add()` even if marshaling fails
- **Simple responsibility**: The codec focuses on serialization mechanics, delegating error handling decisions upstream

This approach is typical for low-level codec implementations that assume callers will handle errors appropriately based on their context.

if isClientCtxErr(stream.Context().Err(), rerr) {

This approach prioritizes **semantic error information** over generic status codes.

# Error Handling Patterns in quota.go

This etcd source file demonstrates several key error handling approaches:

## 1. **Quota Check Pattern**
The `check()` method validates resource availability before operations:
```
"if qa.q.Available(r) { return nil }"
```
If insufficient space exists, it activates an alarm and returns a specific error rather than allowing the operation.

## 2. **Error Propagation**
Methods like `Put()` and `Txn()` follow a consistent pattern:
```
"if err := s.qa.check(ctx, r); err != nil { return nil, err }"
```
They check quotas first, returning early with the error rather than attempting the underlying operation.

## 3. **Typed Error Responses**
The code uses domain-specific errors: `rpctypes.ErrGRPCNoSpace` signals quota exhaustion rather than generic errors, enabling callers to handle resource constraints distinctly.

## 4. **Wrapper Pattern**
`quotaKVServer` and `quotaLeaseServer` wrap underlying servers, injecting quota validation as a cross-cutting concern without modifying core logic.

This design prevents quota violations by failing fast and provides clear, actionable error signals to clients.

# etcd util.go Overview

This Go file from the etcd project contains utility functions for gRPC error handling in the v3 RPC API layer.

## Key Components

**Error Mapping**: The file defines `toGRPCErrorMap`, a comprehensive dictionary that translates internal etcd errors into standardized gRPC error types. This includes errors from membership management, storage (mvcc), authentication, leasing, and version control systems.

**Main Functions**:

1. **togRPCError()** - Converts internal errors to gRPC-compatible errors, allowing context cancellations and deadline exceeded errors to pass through unchanged while mapping others using the error map.

2. **isClientCtxErr()** - Determines whether an error originated from client-side context operations by checking for specific gRPC status codes (Canceled, DeadlineExceeded) and examining error messages for patterns like "client disconnected" or stream cancellations.

3. **isRPCSupportedForLearner()** - Validates which RPC operations learner nodes can execute, permitting StatusRequest calls and serializable RangeRequest operations while rejecting others.

The file uses Apache License 2.0 and imports from Google's gRPC library and etcd's internal packages.

# etcd Error Definitions Overview

This Go file from the etcd project (Apache License 2.0) defines a comprehensive error handling system for gRPC communication.

## Key Components

**Server-Side Errors**: The file declares 60+ error variables using gRPC status codes, including:
- Validation errors: `ErrGRPCEmptyKey`, `ErrGRPCInvalidSortOption`
- Data errors: `ErrGRPCCompacted`, `ErrGRPCNoSpace`
- Authentication errors: `ErrGRPCAuthFailed`, `ErrGRPCInvalidAuthToken`
- Cluster errors: `ErrGRPCNoLeader`, `ErrGRPCClusterIDMismatch`

**Error Mapping**: An `errStringToError` map converts error descriptions to their corresponding error objects, enabling bidirectional error translation.

**Client-Side Wrappers**: Mirror variables without the "GRPC" prefix provide client-facing error definitions.

## Custom Error Type

The `EtcdError` struct wraps gRPC codes and descriptions, implementing error conversion logic through the `Error()` function that translates gRPC errors into etcd-specific error instances.

## Utility Functions

- `ErrorDesc()` extracts message content from status errors
- `Code()` retrieves the underlying gRPC code
- `Error()` performs error lookup and conversion

This design enables consistent error handling across distributed etcd nodes while maintaining compatibility with gRPC's error framework.

# Error Handling Patterns in header.go

Based on the provided content, this file demonstrates **minimal explicit error handling**. The primary pattern observed is:

## Panic-Based Validation

The code uses a panic for nil-checking:

```go
if rh == nil {
    panic("unexpected nil resp.Header")
}
```

This represents a **fail-fast approach** where the function refuses to proceed with invalid state rather than returning an error. The comment "unexpected nil resp.Header" indicates this condition should never occur during normal operation.

## Design Philosophy

The absence of comprehensive error handling suggests this internal RPC package assumes:
- Callers provide valid arguments (contracts enforced upstream)
- The `EtcdServer` instance passed to `newHeader()` is always properly initialized
- Protocol buffer fields are pre-allocated before reaching the `fill()` method

This pattern is common in tightly-integrated internal packages where validation happens at API boundaries, not at every function call.

# HTTP Error Handling Patterns in peer.go

This etcd peer handler demonstrates several error handling approaches:

## Method Validation
The code uses `allowMethod(w, r, "GET")` and `allowMethod(w, r, "POST")` to restrict HTTP verbs, returning early if the method isn't permitted.

## Path Validation
"if r.URL.Path != peerMembersPath { http.Error(w, "bad path"" checks exact path matches, returning `http.StatusBadRequest` for mismatches.

## Parsing with Error Checks
When extracting the member ID from the URL path, `strconv.ParseUint` failures trigger: `http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("member %s not found...", idStr), http.StatusNotFound)`.

## Context-Aware Error Responses
The promote handler reconstructs gRPC metadata from HTTP headers to preserve authentication context before calling business logic.

## Typed Error Matching
Rather than generic error handling, the code uses `errorspkg.Is()` to match specific error types and return appropriate HTTP status codes:
- `ErrIDNotFound` → 404 Not Found
- `ErrMemberNotLearner` → 412 Precondition Failed
- `ErrLearnerNotReady` → 412 Precondition Failed

## Logging with Context
Failed operations log relevant details like member IDs and errors using structured logging (`zap.Logger`).

# Error Message Definition and Error-Related Service Methods

## Error Message Definition

The `ErrorResult` message serves as the primary error structure:

```protobuf
message ErrorResult {
  string message = 1;        // Human-readable description
  string reason = 2;         // Machine-readable status reason
  ErrorDetails details = 3;  // Extended error information
  int32 code = 4;           // Suggested HTTP return code
}
```

Supporting structures include `ErrorDetails` (containing resource identifiers, causes, and retry timing) and `ErrorCause` (describing specific failure reasons with field references).

## Error-Related Service Methods

All service methods return error responses, but no dedicated error-handling methods exist. Instead:

- **ResourceStore** operations (Read, Create, Update, Delete, List, Watch) include `ErrorResult error` fields in their response messages
- **BulkStore.BulkProcess** returns `BulkResponse` containing an `ErrorResult` and a `Rejected` array for failed items
- **ManagedObjectIndex** methods include `ErrorResult error` in responses
- **Quotas.GetQuotaUsage** includes `ErrorResult error` in its response

Each response message independently carries error information rather than through dedicated service methods.
205-usertool_resultWebFetch
# gRPC Error Creation Patterns and Status Code Handling

## Error Creation Patterns

**1. Direct ErrorResult Construction**
```go
ErrOptimisticLockingFailed = resourcepb.ErrorResult{
    Code:    http.StatusConflict,
    Reason:  "optimistic locking failed",
    Message: "requested RV does not match saved RV",
}
```

**2. Helper Functions for Common Errors**
- `NewBadRequestError(msg)` – HTTP 400
- `NewNotFoundError(key)` – HTTP 404 with resource details
- `NewTooManyRequestsError(msg)` – HTTP 429

**3. Field Validation Errors**
The code provides `newInvalidFieldError()` and `newRequiredFieldError()` that attach field-level causes to error responses, enabling detailed validation feedback.

## Status Code Handling

**HTTP Status Mapping:**
The pattern uses standard HTTP status codes (Conflict, BadRequest, NotFound, TooManyRequests, UnprocessableEntity, InternalServerError).

**gRPC Status Conversion:**
The `AsErrorResult()` function converts gRPC status codes to HTTP equivalents via "runtime.HTTPStatusFromCode()," bridging gRPC and REST error semantics.

**Bidirectional Conversion:**
- `AsErrorResult()` transforms Go errors to protobuf ErrorResult
- `GetError()` reconstructs Kubernetes-style StatusError objects from ErrorResult

This approach enables consistent error representation across protocols and frameworks.

# gRPC Method Implementations: Error Handling Analysis

## Create Method
The `Create` method validates the request key and extracts user context before queuing:

```go
func (s *server) Create(ctx context.Context, req *resourcepb.CreateRequest) (*resourcepb.CreateResponse, error)
```

**Error Handling:**
- Returns `http.StatusForbidden` when quota checks fail
- Returns `http.StatusUnauthorized` if user context is missing
- Validates resource key format before processing
- Delegates to internal `create()` which calls `s.newEvent()` for business logic validation

The method wraps operations in `runInQueue()` for QoS handling and applies artificial delays post-success.

## Read Method
The `Read` method retrieves a single resource with authorization checks:

```go
func (s *server) Read(ctx context.Context, req *resourcepb.ReadRequest) (*resourcepb.ReadResponse, error)
```

**Error Handling:**
- Returns `http.StatusUnauthorized` when user is missing
- Returns "missing resource" error if the resource field is empty
- Performs authorization via `s.access.Check()` returning `http.StatusForbidden` on denial
- Returns backend errors directly from `ReadResource()`

## Update Method
Updates enforce optimistic locking and previous version validation:

```go
func (s *server) Update(ctx context.Context, req *resourcepb.UpdateRequest) (*resourcepb.UpdateResponse, error)
```

**Error Handling:**
- Returns `http.StatusUnauthorized` without user context
- Validates `ResourceVersion >= 0`, returning "update must include the previous version" otherwise
- Checks optimistic locking via `rvmanager.IsRvEqual()`, returning `ErrOptimisticLockingFailed` on mismatch
- Uses `newEvent()` for comprehensive validation

# Error Creation Functions and Status Code Patterns

## Error Handling Function

The code defines **`ToDashboardErrorResponse()`** - a single comprehensive error conversion function that maps various error types to HTTP responses with appropriate status codes.

## Status Code Pattern Mapping

| Error Type | Status Code | Pattern |
|---|---|---|
| Dashboard Access Errors | Varies | "Different response status according to the dashboard error type" |
| Folder Not Found | 400 Bad Request | Direct error mapping |
| Plugin Dashboard | 412 Precondition Failed | Returns JSON with status and message |
| Oversized Payload | 413 Payload Too Large | "Dashboard is too large, max is X MB" |
| Kubernetes Status Errors | Variable | Extracted from status error code |
| Unhandled Errors | 500 Internal Server Error | Fallback response |

## Key Patterns Observed

1. **Type Assertion Cascade**: Uses `errors.As()` and `errors.Is()` for error type checking
2. **Custom Response Bodies**: Some errors return structured JSON; others use simple error messages
3. **Context Integration**: Accepts context for plugin name lookup during error processing
4. **Conditional Messaging**: Plugin error messages are enriched by looking up plugin metadata when available

The function prioritizes specific error handling before defaulting to a generic server error response.
231-usertool_resultWebFetch
# Error Handling and HTTP Response Functions

## Error Response Functions

**Error()** - Creates standard error responses with customizable status codes and messages. Handles specific status codes (404, 500) with default messages, settable via the message parameter.

**Err()** - Processes `errutil.Error` types specifically, extracting HTTP status from the error's reason and returning the public-facing error data. Returns 500 Internal Server Error if the error isn't an `errutil.Error`.

**ErrOrFallback()** - Provides fallback behavior by checking if an error is an `errutil.Error` first. If not, it checks for `context.Canceled` and returns a canceled request error, otherwise uses the provided status and message as defaults.

## Standard Response Functions

**Success()** - Generates a 200 OK response containing `{"message": "<provided message>"}`.

**Empty()** - Returns a response with no body content at the specified status code.

**Respond()** - Base response builder that marshals various body types ([]byte, string, nil, or JSON-serializable objects) into responses.

## Specialized Response Functions

**JSON()** / **JSONStreaming()** - Create JSON responses with appropriate content-type headers; streaming variant buffers output for large payloads.

**YAML()** / **YAMLDownload()** - Generate YAML responses using text/yaml or application/yaml with optional download headers.

**JSONDownload()** - JSON response with attachment disposition for file downloads.

**Redirect()** - Produces HTTP 302 redirect responses.

# gRPC Server Initialization, Interceptors, and Error Handling

## Server Initialization

The `provideService` function creates a gRPC server with comprehensive configuration. It instantiates a `gPRCServerService` struct and registers a Prometheus histogram metric for request duration tracking. The server is initialized via `grpc.NewServer(opts...)` after building the options slice.

## Interceptor Setup

The code configures both unary and stream interceptors in a specific order:

**Unary Interceptors:**
- Authentication (if provided)
- Logging with trace ID correlation
- Instrumentation metrics

**Stream Interceptors:**
- Tracing
- Logging
- Instrumentation

The comment notes: *"needs to be registered after tracing interceptor to get trace id"*—indicating intentional ordering for proper correlation.

Authentication is optional and prepended to the chain if an authenticator is supplied, supporting per-service overrides through the `ServiceAuthFuncOverride` interface.

## Error Handling Configuration

The `Run` method implements error handling with:

1. **Listener Setup**: Returns wrapped errors if the network listener fails
2. **Async Serving**: Spawns a goroutine to serve requests, channeling errors
3. **Graceful Shutdown**: Implements context-aware cleanup with a timeout mechanism
4. **Forced Stop**: If graceful shutdown exceeds `GracefulShutdownTimeout`, the server forcefully stops

The shutdown logic uses a goroutine with channel synchronization to enforce the timeout constraint, logging warnings when forced termination occurs.

# Logging Interceptor and Error Handling Patterns

## Logging Interceptor Pattern

The code demonstrates a **conditional logging wrapper** around gRPC interceptors:

```go
func InterceptorLogger(l log.Logger, enabled bool) logging.Logger {
    return logging.LoggerFunc(func(ctx context.Context, lvl logging.Level, msg string, fields ...any) {
        if !enabled {
            return
        }
        // ... logging logic
    })
}
```

This pattern allows toggling logging on/off without replacing interceptors.

## Level-Based Routing

The implementation uses a switch statement to route messages based on severity:

> "case logging.LevelDebug: l.Debug(msg, fields...)"

This approach maps gRPC logging levels (Debug, Info, Warn, Error) to the application's logger methods, maintaining consistency across the logging infrastructure.

## Error Handling Pattern

The code includes defensive programming through a panic case:

> "default: panic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unknown level %v\", lvl))"

This prevents silent failures when unexpected logging levels are encountered, making bugs visible during development.

## Interceptor Registration

Two factory functions provide clean integration points:

- **UnaryServerInterceptor** - handles single request/response calls
- **StreamServerInterceptor** - handles streaming communications

Both accept the same `logger` and `enabled` parameters, ensuring uniform configuration.
251-usertool_resultWebFetch
# Authentication Error Handling in gRPC

## Error Creation Pattern

The code uses `status.Error()` from the gRPC package to generate standardized errors with specific codes and messages:

```go
status.Error(codes.Unauthenticated, "error message")
status.Error(codes.PermissionDenied, "error message")
```

## Key Error Scenarios

**Missing/Invalid Authorization Header:**
- `"no headers in request"` when metadata is absent
- `"no \"authorization\" header in request"` when header missing
- `"malformed \"authorization\" header: one value required"` for incorrect format

**Token Validation Failures:**
- `"missing \"Bearer \" prefix in \"authorization\" value"` 
- `"token required"` for empty tokens
- `"invalid token"` when decoding or lookup fails (logged with specific error details)

**Permission Issues:**
The authenticator enforces specific authorization requirements:
- Service accounts must possess `org.RoleAdmin` status
- Disabled accounts receive: `"service account is disabled"`
- Missing service account associations trigger: `"api key does not have a service account"`
- Non-admin roles are rejected with `"service account does not have admin role"`

## Error Handling Strategy

Authentication errors are caught, logged with context ("token", error details), then converted to generic `Unauthenticated` gRPC responses to avoid leaking sensitive information to clients.

    28→// statusError is an object that can be converted into an metav1.Status
    29→type statusError interface {
    30→	Status() metav1.Status
    31→}
    32→
    33→// ErrorToAPIStatus converts an error to an metav1.Status object.
    34→func ErrorToAPIStatus(err error) *metav1.Status {
    35→	switch t := err.(type) {
    36→	case statusError:
    37→		status := t.Status()
    38→		if len(status.Status) == 0 {
    39→			status.Status = metav1.StatusFailure
    40→		}
    41→		switch status.Status {
    42→		case metav1.StatusSuccess:
    43→			if status.Code == 0 {
    44→				status.Code = http.StatusOK
    45→			}
    46→		case metav1.StatusFailure:
    47→			if status.Code == 0 {
    48→				status.Code = http.StatusInternalServerError
    49→			}
    50→		default:
    51→			runtime.HandleError(fmt.Errorf("apiserver received an error with wrong 
... (truncated)

   207→
   208→// NewForbidden returns an error indicating the requested action was forbidden
   209→func NewForbidden(qualifiedResource schema.GroupResource, name string, err error) *StatusError {
   210→	var message string
   211→	if qualifiedResource.Empty() {
   212→		message = fmt.Sprintf("forbidden: %v", err)
   213→	} else if name == "" {
   214→		message = fmt.Sprintf("%s is forbidden: %v", qualifiedResource.String(), err)
   215→	} else {
   216→		message = fmt.Sprintf("%s %q is forbidden: %v", qualifiedResource.String(), name, err)
   217→	}
   218→	return &StatusError{metav1.Status{
   219→		Status: metav1.StatusFailure,
   220→		Code:   http.StatusForbidden,
   221→		Reason: metav1.StatusReasonForbidden,
   222→		Details: &metav1.StatusDetails{
   223→			Group: qualifiedResource.Group,
   224→			Kind:  qualifiedResource.Resource,
   225→			Name:  name,
   226→		},
   227→		Message: message,
   228→	}}
   229→}
   230→

   238→			Group: qualifiedResource.Group,
   239→			Kind:  qualifiedResource.Resource,
   240→			Name:  name,
   241→		},

   141→var gzipPool = &sync.Pool{
   142→	New: func() interface{} {
   143→		gw, err := gzip.NewWriterLevel(nil, defaultGzipContentEncodingLevel)
   144→		if err != nil {
   145→			panic(err)
   146→		}
   147→		return gw
   148→	},
   149→}
   150→
   151→const (
   152→	// defaultGzipContentEncodingLevel is set to 1 which uses least CPU compared to higher levels, yet offers
   153→	// similar compression ratios (off by at most 1.5x, but typically within 1.1x-1.3x). For further details see -
   154→	// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/112296
   155→	defaultGzipContentEncodingLevel = 1
   156→	// defaultGzipThresholdBytes is compared to the size of the first write from the stream
   157→	// (usually the entire object), and if the size is smaller no gzipping will be performed
   158→	// if the client requests it.
   159→	defaultGzipThresholdBytes = 128 * 1024
   160→	// Use the length of the first write to recognize streaming implementations.
   161→	// When streaming JSON first write is "{", while Kubernetes protobuf starts unique 4 byte header.
   162→	firstWriteStreamingThresholdBytes = 4
   163→)

   174→		return ""
   175→	}

   177→		var token string
   178→		if next := strings.Index(encoding, ",");

   379→// ErrorNegotiated renders an error to the response. Returns the HTTP status code of the error.
   380→// The context is optional and may be nil.
   381→func ErrorNegotiated(err error, s runtime.NegotiatedSerializer, gv schema.GroupVersion, w http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) int {
   382→	status := ErrorToAPIStatus(err)
   383→	code := int(status.Code)
   384→	// when writing an error, check to see if the status indicates a retry after period
   385→	if status.Details != nil && status.Details.RetryAfterSeconds > 0 {
   386→		delay := strconv.Itoa(int(status.Details.RetryAfterSeconds))
   387→		w.Header().Set("Retry-After", delay)
   388→	}
   389→
   390→	if code == http.StatusNoContent {
   391→		w.WriteHeader(code)
   392→		return code
   393→	}
   394→
   395→	WriteObjectNegotiated(s, negotiation.DefaultEndpointRestrictions, gv, w, req, code, status, false)
   396→	return code
   397→}
   398→
   399→// WriteRawJSON writes a non-API object in JSON.
   400→func WriteRawJSON(statusCode int, object interface{}, w http.ResponseWriter) {
   401→	output, err := json.MarshalIndent(object, "", "  ")
   402→	if err != nil {
   403→		http.Error(w, err.Error(), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   404→		return
   405→	}
   406→	w.Header().Set("Content-Type", "application/json")
   407→	w.WriteHeader(statusCode)
   408→	w.Write(output)
   409→}

   824→// ErrorReporter converts generic errors into runtime.Object errors without

   836→// we expect. Because watch is a dependency of the core api, we can't return

   838→// generic error as appropriate. The reason is passed as a unique status cause

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of gRPC error status propagation across the three repositories. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

### **kubernetes/kubernetes**
- **Primary error creation**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors/errors.go` with Kubernetes-specific error constructors (NewNotFound, NewConflict, etc.)
- **gRPC detection**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/rest.go` checks for gRPC status codes via interface detection
- **Translation chain**: ErrorToAPIStatus() → ErrorNegotiated() → HTTP response
- Uses metav1.Status as the unified error model

### **grafana/grafana**
- **gRPC error creation**: `pkg/services/grpcserver/interceptors/auth.go` creates status.Error() with codes.Unauthenticated and codes.PermissionDenied at interceptor level
- **Error messages**: `pkg/storage/unified/resource/errors.go` creates custom error types with embedded HTTP status codes
- **Translation**: Proto-based ErrorResult message embeds HTTP status codes for explicit mapping
- `pkg/api/response/response.go` converts errutil errors to HTTP responses

### **etcd-io/etcd**
- **Centralized error definitions**: `api/v3rpc/rpctypes/error.go` contains 60+ gRPC status error constants
- **Key conversion function**: `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/util.go` has `togRPCError()` function that maps ALL errors via `toGRPCErrorMap`
- **Clean separation**: Domain errors (ErrNoLeader) → gRPC codes (codes.Unavailable) → HTTP codes
- **HTTP translation**: `server/etcdserver/api/etcdhttp/utils.go` has `writeError()` function that translates to HTTP responses

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file listings, key symbols, propagation chains, and a detailed narrative explaining the architectures.

Services\\n\\n### Kubernetes/Kubernetes\\n\\nKubernetes uses a hierarchical error architecture that bridges gRPC status codes to HTTP responses through its API machinery layer.\\n\\n**Error Creation**: The primary error creation functions are in `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors/errors.go`. These functions (NewNotFound, NewConflict, NewInternalError, etc.) create StatusError instances with hardcoded HTTP status codes (404, 409, 500, etc.). These are Kubernetes domain-specific errors, not direct gRPC status codes.\\n\\n**gRPC Error Detection**: In `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/rest.go`, the REST handler explicitly imports gRPC codes and status packages and detects gRPC errors through interface checking. The `isTooLargeError()` function (line 457) checks for both etcd errors (codes.InvalidArgument with \\\"request is too large\\\" message) and gRPC errors (codes.ResourceExhausted). This detection happens at the request scope level.\\n\\n**Error Translation Chain**: The translation path flows through three main stages:\\n1. Error creation or detection (NewNotFound, isTooLargeError)\\n2. Conversion to metav1.Status via `ErrorToAPIStatus()` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/responsewriters/status.go`, which maps gRPC status codes to HTTP codes (lines 34-83)\\n3. HTTP response rendering via `ErrorNegotiated()` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/responsewriters/writers.go`\\n\\n**CRI Integration**: The Kubelet's Container Runtime Interface has dedicated error handling in `staging/src/k8s.io/kubelet/pkg/cri/streaming/errors.go`, where `WriteError()` directly translates gRPC codes (codes.NotFound \u2192 404, codes.ResourceExhausted \u2192 429) to HTTP responses for streaming endpoints.\\n\\n**gRPC Rate Limiting**: `pkg/kubelet/apis/grpc/ratelimit.go` creates gRPC status errors directly via `status.Error(codes.ResourceExhausted, ...)` for rate limiting scenarios, handled by the LimiterUnaryServerInterceptor.\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana\\n\\nGrafana implements error handling at multiple layers with explicit gRPC code usage in interceptors and protobuf-based error response structures.\\n\\n**gRPC Interceptor Level**: In `pkg/services/grpcserver/interceptors/auth.go`, authentication errors are created using `status.Error(codes.Unauthenticated, ...)` and `status.Error(codes.PermissionDenied, ...)` directly at the unary/stream interceptor level. These are created early in the request pipeline before any business logic executes.\\n\\n**Resource Server Error Layer**: The unified resource storage layer (`pkg/storage/unified/resource/errors.go`) provides error constructors like `NewBadRequestError()` and `NewNotFoundError()` that create custom error types. These include HTTP status codes directly in the error definition. The `AsErrorResult()` function converts errors to protobuf ErrorResult messages with explicit HTTP status codes embedded.\\n\\n**Resource Server Operations**: Files like `pkg/storage/unified/resource/server.go` implement CRUD operations (Create, Read, Update, Delete) that return errors with HTTP status codes. These errors bubble up to the HTTP layer.\\n\\n**HTTP Response Translation**: In `pkg/api/response/response.go`, the `Err()` function extracts HTTP status from errutil.Error types and renders them as HTTP responses. The `ErrOrFallback()` function handles context.Canceled errors and falls back to default status codes when needed.\\n\\n**Dashboard Error Mapping**: The `pkg/api/apierrors/dashboard.go` file contains `ToDashboardErrorResponse()` function that comprehensively maps various error types (including Kubernetes API errors and plugin errors) to HTTP responses using type assertions and error comparisons.\\n\\n**Proto Definition**: `pkg/storage/unified/proto/resource.proto` defines ErrorResult message with fields for HTTP status code suggestion, making the gRPC-to-HTTP mapping explicit in the protocol definition.\\n\\n### etcd-io/etcd\\n\\netcd uses a clear two-layer error system: domain errors that map to gRPC status errors via a centralized conversion function, which can then be translated to HTTP.\\n\\n**Error Definition Layer**: `api/v3rpc/rpctypes/error.go` is the primary error definition file containing 60+ gRPC status error constants (ErrGRPCEmptyKey with codes.InvalidArgument, ErrGRPCKeyNotFound with codes.NotFound, ErrGRPCNoLeader with codes.Unavailable, ErrGRPCInvalidAuthToken with codes.PermissionDenied, etc.). The `Error()` function converts gRPC errors to EtcdError structs, and `ErrorDesc()` extracts messages.\\n\\n**Domain Error Layer**: `server/etcdserver/errors/errors.go` defines domain-specific errors (ErrNoLeader, ErrStopped, ErrTimeout, ErrCanceled) that are internal to the server implementation and don't directly use gRPC codes.\\n\\n**Centralized Conversion**: `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/util.go` contains the critical `togRPCError()` function that maps all internal errors to gRPC status errors via the `toGRPCErrorMap`. This is the single point where domain errors become gRPC errors. The function distinguishes between client context errors (which pass through) and server errors (which get mapped).\\n\\n**RPC Handler Usage**: Multiple RPC handler files use togRPCError for conversion:\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/key.go`: Key-value operations\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/auth.go`: Authentication operations\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/lease.go`: Lease operations\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/member.go`: Cluster member operations\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/watch.go`: Watch stream operations\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/quota.go`: Storage quota enforcement\\n- `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/maintenance.go`: Maintenance operations\\n\\n**HTTP Translation**: `server/etcdserver/api/etcdhttp/utils.go` contains `writeError()` function that translates errors to HTTP responses. It handles both v2error.Error types and generic errors, mapping them to appropriate HTTP status codes.\\n\\n**HTTP Peer Endpoints**: `server/etcdserver/api/etcdhttp/peer.go` uses `allowMethod()` for HTTP verb validation (returns 405) and maps specific error types to HTTP codes using error.Is() checks (e.g., ErrIDNotFound \u2192 404, ErrMemberNotLearner \u2192 412).\\n\\n**gRPC Server Configuration**: `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/grpc.go` sets up the gRPC server with appropriate message size limits and interceptors, establishing the infrastructure where gRPC status codes are created and propagated.\\n\\n**gRPC Interceptors**: `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/interceptor.go` validates capabilities and returns errors like rpctypes.ErrGRPCNotCapable early in the request chain, ensuring errors are caught before expensive operations.\\n\\n### Comparative Analysis\\n\\n**Kubernetes** creates Kubernetes-specific error types (not direct gRPC codes) that include HTTP status codes, detecting gRPC errors from external services and converting them through ErrorToAPIStatus().\\n\\n**Grafana** uses explicit gRPC status codes at the interceptor level combined with protobuf-based error messages that embed HTTP status codes, making the translation point explicit in the proto definition.\\n\\n**etcd** maintains a clean separation: domain errors \u2192 centralized togRPCError() conversion \u2192 HTTP translation via writeError(). This design makes error mapping explicit and auditable in a single location (toGRPCErrorMap).\\n\\nAll three projects handle the fundamental challenge of bridging gRPC's status code system with HTTP status codes, but they do so at different architectural layers: Kubernetes at the API server layer, Grafana through protobuf-embedded status codes, and etcd through explicit conversion mapping.\"\n}\n",
